class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, June 3, 2024 3:26 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1247255035210104904>6/3/2024 3:26 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, June 3, 2024 3:26 PM">3:26 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>from what i can tell, dbt generally recommends going with the imperfect approach, but re-running all your incrementally-built from scratch on a schedule, to avoid drift over a longer priod of time</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1247273656690802814 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1247273656690802814><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/984386111709253672/23fac11e09942718016d6d4c58935a2e.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rebirch data-user-id=984386111709253672>reBirch</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, June 3, 2024 4:40 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1247273656690802814>6/3/2024 4:40 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I (shortly will) need to design an ETL pipeline. I&#39;ll describe the context, and how I intend to solve it. Any and all criticisms welcome.
<ul><li>The company is firmly wedded to AWS as a cloud provider, there is nothing on-prem. Open-source services can be used, however, something that will require a lot of effort in maintenance from Infra is unwelcome. Additional vendors are out of the picture.</li><li>We have some data that is incoming to an s3 bucket. It is coming infrequently, something like once every 2 days. The data is always 1 file (100s of MB) in a fairly exotic format. This part cannot be changed. A new file appearing on the s3 bucket should trigger the execution of our pipeline. </li><li>We have some logic that my team&#39;s analysts have written. It is able to open and read this exotic-format file, enrich the data from there with information from some additional sources (all of which are accessed via REST APIs), and then run an (also fairly exotic) ML model on it to classify it. The logic is stateful - in cases where it cannot classify, it looks up similar records from its own output (more about output storage in a minute) to try classifying it again. Then, the results are written to the output storage. This can process a single pipeline-triggering batch of data in a few hours.</li><li>The output storage can be anything, the team is using some RDS db now, but they are not wedded to it being relational, or a database at all, and the choice of database they used up to now was not driven by any kind of serious decision-making process. It must support writes of the output of the pipeline (so, infrequent big writes), the pipeline looking up specific records it couldn&#39;t classify (infrequent periods of frequent small reads) and the downstream consumers of data reading the output (infrequent big reads).</li><li>While the pipeline is stateful, the ML model that sits at the heart of the data processing logic does not need to be re-trained in production.</li></ul></span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Monday, June 3, 2024 4:44 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1247277479408832584 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1247277479408832584><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/984386111709253672/23fac11e09942718016d6d4c58935a2e.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rebirch data-user-id=984386111709253672>reBirch</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, June 3, 2024 4:55 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1247277479408832584>6/3/2024 4:55 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>How I intend to approach it:
<ul><li>Triggering the execution can happen through EventBridge, or through Airflow with an S3FileSensor operator.</li><li>The pipeline could be orchestrated with probably Airflow. It could be a very small Lambda (this is questionable, see below) or AWS Batch, too. </li><li>The data processing logic involves a lot of stuff that doesn&#39;t lend itself well or easily to distributed processing with things like Spark or Ray. So, we probably need a single big EC2 instance. Once triggered, the orchestrating service will use boto3 to start the instance, and execute the pipeline logic (wrapped into a Python package) on it, passing the key of the newly uploaded file as a parameter. After completing the run, the instance will be shut down. </li><li>Models probably can be served as pickles on a separate s3 bucket. The pipeline package will unpickle the model from this s3 and use it during the run.</li><li>About the output storage, I have no idea right now. I think if the team and our downstream consumers are happy with the RDS they ended up with, we could do a POC with that, and then look for other options if performance and cost demand it.</li></ul></span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Monday, June 3, 2024 6:42 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1247278256864886815 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1247278256864886815><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/113136451457146880/0275ef289c9e7b6338d7b72e8f4f2fca.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=i_._i data-user-id=113136451457146880>dean</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, June 3, 2024 4:58 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1247278256864886815>6/3/2024 4:58 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Seems reasonable at first glance to me given what I know about your company and data (nothing) but I would encourage you to look at ECS Fargate tasks instead of EC2 if you plan on building up/tearing down your instance every time.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1247278434552385567 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1247278434552385567><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/984386111709253672/23fac11e09942718016d6d4c58935a2e.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rebirch data-user-id=984386111709253672>reBirch</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, June 3, 2024 4:59 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1247278434552385567>6/3/2024 4:59 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Aren&#39;t you very limited in terms of specifying what compute you get with Fargate?</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1247768750040809483 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1247768750040809483><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/710197941620703324/508e12e7aec4e4b88b707472a8d4c1d2.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/423971764431749120/0ba8c122ad65827204786c85b9124b41.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=kaizen_spr>kaizen</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1247695502745534536')"> What’s the best way to delete a user and everything associated with them from every table and database </span> <span class=chatlog__reply-edited-timestamp title="Tuesday, June 4, 2024 8:36 PM">(edited)</span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=xxrusxsniperxx data-user-id=710197941620703324>xXRuSXSnIpERXx</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, June 5, 2024 1:27 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1247768750040809483>6/5/2024 1:27 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Depending on how the database is setup, cascading foreign keys are going to be your friend here.  However, I would caution that deleting anything that is a primary/foreign key, especially across databases is quite cumbersome.  Most of the time, if you can simply null out a record/obfuscate the record, that will be much more preferable.  The other reason is that depending on the case, there are some cases where deleting records causes problem.  The simplest example I can think of is purchase records.  If you delete the user and all their associated records, you are deleting financial data as well, indicating that you didn&#39;t receive revenue from that user, which is not true.  In short, for PII related stuff, it&#39;s almost always preferable to obfuscate the record and move on.  Willing to hear other opinions though.</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=100><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=💯 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f4af.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1247772648721743954 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1247772648721743954><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/423971764431749120/0ba8c122ad65827204786c85b9124b41.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/710197941620703324/508e12e7aec4e4b88b707472a8d4c1d2.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=xxrusxsniperxx>xXRuSXSnIpERXx</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1247768750040809483')"> Depending on how the database is setup, cascading foreign keys are going to be your friend here.  However, I would caution that deleting anything that is a primary/foreign key, especially across databases is quite cumbersome.  Most of the time, if you can simply null out a record/obfuscate the record, that will be much more preferable.  The other reason is that depending on the case, there are some cases where deleting records causes problem.  The simplest example I can think of is purchase records.  If you delete the user and all their associated records, you are deleting financial data as well, indicating that you didn&#39;t receive revenue from that user, which is not true.  In short, for PII related stuff, it&#39;s almost always preferable to obfuscate the record and move on.  Willing to hear other opinions though. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=kaizen_spr data-user-id=423971764431749120>kaizen</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, June 5, 2024 1:43 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1247772648721743954>6/5/2024 1:43 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>That’s exactly what I have been thinking to do. Looking through through primary keys and just update the tables with space “” or a character</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Wednesday, June 5, 2024 1:47 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1247784758163931197 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1247784758163931197><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/710197941620703324/508e12e7aec4e4b88b707472a8d4c1d2.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=xxrusxsniperxx data-user-id=710197941620703324>xXRuSXSnIpERXx</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, June 5, 2024 2:31 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1247784758163931197>6/5/2024 2:31 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I personally hate the empty string in the database.  At my job, there have been plenty of times where an empty string got persisted to the database because it was not-nullable but the value was never updated from an empty string.  You could set blank values if you want to but you may want to pick something identifiable like &quot;<strong>REMOVED</strong>&quot; or something to that effect.  I could also see it being used for analysis, such as if you wanted to see how many users requested their data to be deleted, you could just do a count(*) where name = <strong>REMOVED</strong>, for example.  Just something that is up to you, mostly personal preference</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1247785098678370355 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1247785098678370355><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Wednesday, June 5, 2024 2:32 AM">2:32 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>It&#39;s also easier to make sure that it&#39;s not just a user who didn&#39;t provide a name for example and your application just persists the empty string, like I mentioned.  It&#39;s a valid user record but there may be fields that are blank because the user didn&#39;t provide something and your application enforces non-nullability</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1247785667635970059 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1247785667635970059><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Wednesday, June 5, 2024 2:34 AM">2:34 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Technically as well, since there is a distinction (with the exception of Oracle) between &quot;&quot; and null, you could view those values as different.  NULL could represent that you simply don&#39;t have the data, such as if you imported records or the data is just absent for whatever reason whereas &quot;&quot; means they explicitly didn&#39;t provide it.  I personally don&#39;t like the empty string because I don&#39;t really see a valuable distinction between those two interpretations but it&#39;s really up to you.  Not trying to be pedantic but I have run into this exact question before so I figured I&#39;d offer what I prefer, even if you may prefer something different</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1248321464172544100 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1248321464172544100><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=armslegshandsfeet data-user-id=466248882335252500>armslegshandsfeet</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, June 6, 2024 2:03 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1248321464172544100>6/6/2024 2:03 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>The thing about Iceberg and all of the table formats is that they&#39;re really just specifications that have to be implemented; it&#39;s not really a service like Airflow.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1248321767987089408 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1248321767987089408><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 6, 2024 2:05 PM">2:05 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Right now, the spec&#39;s most fully implemented in Spark, but there&#39;s also support in Dremio and Trino. There&#39;s limited support in Python, BigQuery, Redshift (?), and Snowflake.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1248322169692491839 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1248322169692491839><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 6, 2024 2:06 PM">2:06 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Where Tabular steps in is in providing a REST catalog implementation and managed catalog maintenance, since the metadata catalog is one of the key components to how Iceberg (and all the table formats) know which files belong to which tables and versions of tables.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1248322421484687411 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1248322421484687411><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 6, 2024 2:07 PM">2:07 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I don&#39;t have hands-on with Glue or Hive, but my understanding is that the snapshot pruning and file compaction operations are 100% manual there, or you have to roll your own management system to automate the tasks.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1248323506857574512 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1248323506857574512><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, June 6, 2024 2:11 PM">2:11 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>But yeah. tldr is that the Tabular peeps are Iceberg founders and contributed ~30% of the code base. Sorry for the rant.
I feel like I&#39;ve kind of painted myself into a corner, career-wise. At the risk of discrediting the cases where I write something here with an authoritative tone - I am not that experienced. I am self-taught, I have worked a total of 3 years and change as a DA (although I did some DE tasks as a DA), and a year as a DE. I kind of lucked my way into a DE role - the team was going through a reorganization, and I pitched to my manager an idea of &quot;hey, I already do a lot of engineering work - do you feel like there is a place for a dedicated engineer role in the team now?&quot;. He agreed, and I went from a mid DA to a mid DE overnight - there were no tests, no interviews, nothing. 
Back then, the team was focused on customer reports. They had no SLA and limited scope, so becoming an &quot;engineer&quot; for this team was easy - I just built Spark and Python jobs and AF dags, and helped people out with git. 
Since then, the team&#39;s scope shifted - a C-level got green light for a pet project, and for a bit less than a year now, we have abandoned reports and develop it as a &quot;startup within a company&quot;. I am still the only engineer in the team - we have a single very junior product manager, and a few DA and DS. 
I find that I am forced to wear a very large number of hats. I am my own project manager, and I basically own coordinating with other technical teams - like infra, downstream dependent products, upstream products we depend on, etc. There is no one who understands the dependencies like I do, and the roadmaps my team lead and product manager come up with have no bearing on reality because of that. I end up owning the entire roadmap from the moment a feature&#39;s business logic is written by DAs, up until production. I make the architecture/tool choice decisions that I have very little competence in making, and at this point senior engineers in other teams, to whom I constantly run for advice, are getting sick of critiquing my architecture diagrams.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Monday, June 17, 2024 5:06 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1252736170094366820 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1252736170094366820><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/984386111709253672/23fac11e09942718016d6d4c58935a2e.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/216277831326367744/a9dc4b8c74871c103470dc2b7935dc32.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=kkiks>Kkiks</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1252589057687420938')"> Really random one and less of a DE one -

We have quite a few different departments that all work with PowerBI and develop their own reports for stakeholders etc. All fun and games, but they all look so different; directors are a bit annoyed that if a combined report of all of them gets put together, it looks like its an absolute puzzle pieced together, rather than a coherent thing. Does anybody have much experience with standardisation of reports and how do you deal with that in your company? Is it more of a practice of developing one report that just goes to senior stakeholders or is it more alignment of the various departments and their practices, or both? </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rebirch data-user-id=984386111709253672>reBirch</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, June 18, 2024 6:26 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1252736170094366820>6/18/2024 6:26 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>We went through it. Ultimately I agree with <span class="chatlog__markdown-mention" title="kahnwong">@kahnwong</span> 
<div class="chatlog__markdown-quote"><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-border"></div><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-content">(This is not a technical problem)
</div></div>It is more of a Conway&#39;s law problem. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conway%27s_law">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conway%27s_law</a>
The solution was in our company&#39;s case quite heavy-handed - management just formed a single &quot;BI reporting&quot; team and made them own all of the reports everybody else did previously, so it all got implemented in a similar style.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Tuesday, June 18, 2024 6:27 PM">(edited)</span></div><div class=chatlog__embed><div class="chatlog__embed-color-pill chatlog__embed-color-pill--default"></div><div class=chatlog__embed-content-container><div class=chatlog__embed-content><div class=chatlog__embed-text><div class=chatlog__embed-title><a class=chatlog__embed-title-link href=https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conway%27s_law><div class="chatlog__markdown chatlog__markdown-preserve">Conway&#39;s law</div></a></div><div class=chatlog__embed-description><div class="chatlog__markdown chatlog__markdown-preserve">Conway&#39;s law describes the link between communication structure of organizations and the systems they design. It is named after the computer programmer Melvin Conway, who introduced the idea in 1967. His original wording was:

[O]rganizations which design systems (in the broad sense used here) are constrained to produce designs which are copies ...</div></div></div></div></div></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=100><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=💯 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f4af.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1256649175513174106 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1256649175513174106><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/984386111709253672/23fac11e09942718016d6d4c58935a2e.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rebirch data-user-id=984386111709253672>reBirch</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, June 29, 2024 1:35 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1256649175513174106>6/29/2024 1:35 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>The deployment is hairier since you need to point to the file to install the package on a cluster, and wheels include the version in the filename (I&#39;m coming from a Python-centric perspective here, maybe R and Scala people have it easier, IDK). The options around this that I know of:
<ul><li> deploy the wheel file somewhere like an s3 (or dbfs, but I don&#39;t like the mess that it becomes). Manually update the reference to the whl file in your databricks assets. Accept that the deployment process is manual to an extent. This is ugly but works if you don&#39;t have that many Databricks assets (e.g. my team maintained a large number of ETL pipelines that all used the same Databricks job as &quot;entrypoint&quot;, but were actually orchestrated by different AF DAGs).</li><li>(An improvement on the previous option) Same as before package and upload your whl somewhere, but also define your databricks stuff in your repo and deploy with an asset bundle. Updating the reference to the whl in your databricks asset definition is done dynamically as part of the CD job (jinja templates, just file editing, etc).</li><li>Use a private package index like Artifactory, and install from it onto your cluster. How to do this is messy and will probably involve working with your infra team to dynamically modify cluster policies, or use init scripts, or something like that.</li></ul></span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Saturday, June 29, 2024 1:37 PM">(edited)</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1256650372559147048 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1256650372559147048><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, June 29, 2024 1:39 PM">1:39 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>(We used &quot;Python Wheel&quot; type tasks for all jobs everywhere. It&#39;s pretty neat as it lets you package all of the code inside the wheel and define the runnable entry point, unlike python-based spark-submit which needs a separate executable file.)</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Saturday, June 29, 2024 1:41 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

)

  ssc,
  LocationStrategies.PreferConsistent,
  ConsumerStrategies.Subscribe[String, String](topics, kafkaParams)
)

stream.foreachRDD { rdd =&gt;
  val dataRDD = rdd.map(record =&gt; read[IoTData](record.value()))
  val groupedByArrondissementRDD = dataRDD
    .map(data =&gt; (data.arrondissement, List(data)))
    .reduceByKey(_ ++ _)
 
  groupedByArrondissementRDD.foreach {
    case (arrondissement, peopleIterable) =&gt;
    val peopleList = peopleIterable.toList
    val urgenceCases = findUrgenceCase(peopleList)
    // SOME CODE
    }
  }

ssc.start()
ssc.awaitTermination()

I assume they are creating a platform that does prompt engineering for their clients using chatgpt api on a RAG architecture </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=apatheticlamp data-user-id=114858490555531268>Lamp - Databricks #1 fan</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, June 30, 2024 2:46 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1257029528501358593>6/30/2024 2:46 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Imo, LLM based AI is the <em>hardest</em> field
Other ML based spaces are usually a bit easier to evaluate. Think about a classifier, it tells you fraud or not fraud. It&#39;s either right or wrong and you can get to a ground truth, it&#39;s still kinda hard though, unless you have good data and labels.

Now think about LLMs, you put in input and get language output, how do you tell it&#39;s right? You need a bunch of experts to sit there and evaluate LLM outputs. What if your output isn&#39;t quite right? Is it the LLM, or did you prompt it poorly. Now you need to A/B test a bunch of prompts with your expert.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Sunday, June 30, 2024 2:46 PM">(edited)</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=100><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=💯 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f4af.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1257029777987211376 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1257029777987211376><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Sunday, June 30, 2024 2:47 PM">2:47 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Imo, that startup is just looking to get acquired, that&#39;s the exit strategy</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1257029968584507452 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1257029968584507452><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Sunday, June 30, 2024 2:48 PM">2:48 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Only reason I&#39;d join is because it&#39;s my only offer and I need a job</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1257844827148517507 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1257844827148517507><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/448299508162625546/47636d751fdb1d2989eaa3c565f0447d.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=mochathecat6 data-user-id=448299508162625546>mochathecat6</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, July 2, 2024 8:46 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1257844827148517507>7/2/2024 8:46 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Hi, I am seeking career advice as I am currently stuck in my Data Engineering career. I was hired as the only DE on an AI team of a SaaS company in Toronto 3 years ago. In the first 1.5 years of my career, I was responsible for creating Airflow DAGs, moving data into Snowflake, creating Python functions for Data Scientists to fetch data, and building AWS cloud infrastructure using Terraform. However, our data is very clean, so it doesn’t need much transformation or cleaning.

After the first 1.5 years, my focus shifted to building AWS infrastructure and creating CI/CD pipelines for the team and the AI apps. I’ve become the DevOps guy on the team. Most of my knowledge and skills in DE are self-taught (Spark, Kafka, DE architecture design, and modeling). However, I know that I lack real-world experience in solving complex DE problems. I have been applying to jobs since January 2024 and have interviewed at around 10 companies. I was able to reach the live coding round with 7 of them and I reached final round with 5 of them. I got 1 offer(didn’t accept it)

I can talk about DE projects and DE architecture design without any problem (never failed this round). I have also never failed the Python and SQL round (did 500+ LeetCode problems combined). However, I have failed 3 interviews on data modeling, the ones where they ask you to actually model the tables.

I have the following questions regarding my future career:

    1.    Should I build my skill set based on what my current team is using?

Basically making your work not re-useable in the new solutions? </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rebirch data-user-id=984386111709253672>reBirch</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, July 3, 2024 10:34 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1258053220551364669>7/3/2024 10:34 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I was in the exactly the same position as you. Worked on a big migration project for over a year, then it got scrapped. There&#39;s nothing that you can do when you&#39;re in this position in the hierarchy, for this particular project. Next time, it may help to do EXTENSIVE discovery when you&#39;re starting out the project, to make sure the tool you&#39;re about to commit to is not &quot;on its way out&quot;. You senior Infra people and architects are the best people to talk to about this.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1258053655492558881 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1258053655492558881><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Wednesday, July 3, 2024 10:36 AM">10:36 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Also, make sure you have a project lined up that your manager will shuffle you into after your current one is scrapped. As in, make sure your manager doesn&#39;t see you solely as &quot;the guy responsible for that project&quot;. 

I don&#39;t think this is widespread, so I don&#39;t want to worry you too much, but you could end up &quot;on the bench&quot; after your current project is scrapped, and then be on your way on on the next layoff. (N=1, but for the record, that didn&#39;t happen to me.)</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Wednesday, July 3, 2024 10:37 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1259034932580454442 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1259034932580454442><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/313937749042528259/3c45f1f8fc49903e78f32160d2ac4224.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=iratedownloader data-user-id=313937749042528259>iratedownloader</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, July 6, 2024 3:35 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1259034932580454442>7/6/2024 3:35 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Ya folks...I&#39;m just wondering.

Spark is such a commonly used tool for data transformation....but why?

Assuming we have a data warehouse like BigQuery, what my org does is that we bring the data &quot;as is&quot; in the source to BigQuery using Kafka/Spark, then do any complex transformation within BigQuery.

Even if a table has million rows and 100 columns and I want to do a complex transformation using window functions or something, BigQuery would be able to do it within a minute in on-demand mode. Spark would take probably &gt; 1 hour, not to mention the optimization stuff we would have to do in the code with re-partition, broadcast variables etc.

So given this, why would an org do data transformation in spark over a data warehouse? The thing is, I&#39;m giving a lot of interviews for DE recently &amp; the consistent pattern is that, any interviewer that decides to deep dive way too much into spark, I get screwed lol since we do all our complex transformations in BigQuery and not Spark.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Saturday, July 6, 2024 3:36 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

If the private key is exposed then you have access just like if the password does </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=i_._i data-user-id=113136451457146880>dean</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, July 14, 2024 5:24 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1262142790893174804>7/14/2024 5:24 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I&#39;d still say yes. In addition to the much higher entropy compared to your average password (especially since snowflake caps PWs at 256 chars) SSH-based auth doesn&#39;t actually need to transmit the private key to the server, only prove that it has it. You can also add a password second factor as an extra step.
